Rulings on Crescent Testimony for Ramadan and Shawwal
Conditions for accepting crescent testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting testimony for the crescents of Ramadan and Shawwal according to the Hanafi school, distinguish between the requirements for cloudy and clear weather, and explain the legal basis for these rulings.

Core Idea
Crescent testimony rules balance ease (one witness in cloudy Ramadan) with caution (multitude in clear, two for Shawwal).

Determining the start and end of Ramadan is a communal obligation that rests on credible testimony. The Hanafi school has detailed conditions for accepting such testimony, taking into account the difficulty of sighting and the importance of certainty. This lesson unpacks the passage from al-Hidayah that sets these rules, focusing on witness qualifications, required numbers, and the role of weather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
The act is testimony (shahada) given before a judge regarding the sighting of the crescent. This testimony establishes the beginning or end of Ramadan and is treated as a religious matter combining divine and human rights.
Unlike civil lawsuits, no formal claim (da'wa) is required.
2
Specify the conditions of the witness
The witness must be 'adl (upright), which means not a manifest sinner. Even a slave, a woman, or a person flogged for slander who has repented is acceptable. An unrepentant sinner (fasiq) is rejected based on Quran 49:6.
A person of unknown status (mastur al-hal) is considered trustworthy.
3
Distinguish between Ramadan and Shawwal
For the start of Ramadan (sawm), if the sky is cloudy, one upright witness suffices. For the end of Ramadan (Shawwal, iftar), two men or one man and two women are required. In clear weather, a great multitude (number left to judge's discretion) is required for both.
The exception for cloudy Ramadan is based on necessity and prophetic practice.
4
Examine the wording and procedural requirements
The testimony must be given using the word 'ashhadu (I testify) to emphasize its legal force. No lawsuit is needed because the matter involves divine rights.
This distinguishes crescent testimony from purely civil claims.
5
Handle the scenario after 30 days of fasting
If two upright witnesses testified to Ramadan and the community fasted 30 days, they may break the fast at the end of 30 days even if the Shawwal crescent is not seen, because the month cannot exceed 30 days. There is a difference of opinion among later scholars about the case where the initial testimony was in clear weather.
Al-Marghinani supports the general permissibility; Ibn al-Humam restricts it.

On condition that he is upright, even if a slave, or a woman, or one who was flogged for slander but has repented. And for breaking the fast, it is required [that there be] two men, or one man and two women, and the wording 'I testify' not 'lawsuit'. And without clouds, a great multitude is required in both.

[1] His saying: 'upright' means not a manifest sinner; if his state is unknown, his word is accepted, as in al-Hidayah.
[2] His saying: 'who has repented' means if he did not repent, he is a sinner whose statement is not accepted in religious matters, due to His saying: 'If a sinner comes to you with news, verify it.'
[3] His saying: 'and the wording 'I testify'' — indeed the prescribed number of witnesses is required, and the wording 'I testify' because it has the force of testimony. And the lawsuit is not required because it is not purely the right of a servant, but rather there is the right of Allah in it as well, and the lawsuit is only in purely personal rights.
[4] His saying: 'a great multitude' — the outward meaning indicates what reaches the number of tawatur that yields certain knowledge, but it is not so; rather it means the multitude from whose report a preponderant probability is obtained, and it is left to the judge's opinion without specifying a number, and this is the correct view. And a trustworthy scholar in a town where there is no judge stands in his place.
[5] His saying: 'and after fasting thirty days with the statement of two upright persons, breaking the fast becomes permissible' — meaning when two [witnesses] testify to the crescent of Ramadan, and the judge rules to fast based on their testimony, and they fast thirty days, then after its completion it becomes permissible for them to break the fast, whether the crescent of Shawwal is seen or not, because the month does not exceed thirty days, and Ramadan has been established by the required number of witnesses considered in legal matters.
[6] His saying: 'breaking the fast becomes permissible' — if the sky on the night of the thirty-first is cloudy, this is by agreement. And if it is clear and the crescent of Shawwal is not seen, then similarly according to what is corrected in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah, but its opposite is corrected in Majmu' al-Nawazil. Ibn al-Humam chose that if he accepted it in clear weather (i.e., regarding the crescent of Ramadan) and the number is complete, they do not break the fast; and if he accepted it in clouds, they break the fast.
[7] His saying: 'obstruction' with a kasra on the 'ayn and shadda on the lam means a hindrance to sighting, like clouds.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the Hanafi conditions for accepting testimony regarding the crescents of Ramadan and Shawwal. The author begins by stating the general condition of 'adl (uprightness) for witnesses, emphasizing that a slave, a woman, or a person who was flogged for slander but repented are acceptable. Then he distinguishes between the testimony for the start of Ramadan and for the end of it (Shawwal). For the start of Ramadan, testimony of one upright witness is sufficient if there is an obstruction (clouds) – this is an exception to the usual two-witness requirement, based on necessity and ease. For the end of Ramadan (Shawwal), two men or one man and two women are required, and the witness must use the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) to emphasize the legal force. The commentary clarifies that the word 'adl means not being a manifest sinner (fasiq); a person of unknown status is accepted. The Quranic verse from Surah al-Hujurat is cited to reject the testimony of an unrepentant sinner. The commentary also explains why a lawsuit (da'wa) is not required here: this is a religious matter involving both divine and human rights, unlike purely civil suits. Regarding the number of witnesses in clear weather, the text requires a 'great multitude' – the commentary explains this as a number that yields a preponderance of probability, left to the judge's discretion, not a fixed number like tawatur. The passage then addresses a practical scenario: if two witnesses testified to the start of Ramadan, and the community fasted thirty days, then it becomes permissible to break the fast at the end of thirty days even if the Shawwal crescent is not seen, because the month cannot exceed 30 days. There is a difference of opinion among later authorities about the case when the sky was clear at the beginning (and one witness was accepted due to clouds? Actually, the text says if they accepted testimony in clear weather for Ramadan, then after thirty days they should not break fast? This is a nuanced ikhtilaf. The correct position according to the author is that if the original testimony for Ramadan was accepted in cloudy weather, they break; if in clear weather, they do not. The passage concludes by defining 'illa (obstruction) as anything preventing sighting, like clouds.

Key Terms
عدل (adl): One who is not a manifest fasiq; if his state is unknown (mastur al-hal), his word is accepted in this context.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, such as an unrepentant slanderer (qadhif). His testimony is rejected.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given with the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) before a judge; it requires the prescribed number of witnesses.
دعوى (da'wa): A formal claim or lawsuit; not required for crescent testimony because it involves both divine and human rights.
علة (illa): An obstruction that prevents sighting the crescent, such as clouds, dust, or fog.
جمع عظيم (jam' 'azim): A great multitude whose report yields a preponderance of probability; not a fixed number, left to the judge's opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One upright man or woman
B) Two men or one man and two women
C) A great multitude of any number
D) Fifty men

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts one upright witness for the Ramadan crescent only when there is an obstruction (clouds), requires a multitude in clear weather, and uses stricter requirements for the Shawwal crescent to ensure certainty in ending the fast.

Moon Sighting Testimony: When Does a Single Witness Suffice?
Commentary on the number of witnesses for moon sighting and the intra-Hanafi dispute on ending Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a single witness is accepted for Ramadan and apply the majority Hanafi position to determine when the fast ends.

Core Idea
A single witness suffices for Ramadan only under cloud cover; ending the fast requires either sighting or two witnesses except in Muhammad's view.

The Hanafi school permits accepting a single just witness's testimony to begin Ramadan, but only when the sky is cloudy. What happens after 30 days? Can the same witness's implied testimony end the fast? The classical commentators expand on this, revealing a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the majority of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The dispute centers on whether a single witness's testimony, accepted to start Ramadan under cloud cover, also suffices to end the fast after 30 days without a new sighting or additional witnesses.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the end of Ramadan is a separate worldly benefit requiring the same evidentiary standard as other rights: two witnesses or actual sighting. A single witness does not establish the end.
They analogize iftar to other rights of servants, not purely religious.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's counter-argument
Imam Muhammad argues that if the start was validated by one witness, then the end follows implicitly (tab'an) from completion of 30 days. He compares it to a midwife's testimony establishing lineage leading to inheritance.
The inheritance is not established directly by the midwife but by her testimony's consequence.
4
Examine the majority's response
The majority reject the analogy: inheritance is never directly proven by one woman's testimony, whereas here the end of fasting is directly claimed. The start and end are distinct rulings; the completion of 30 days does not automatically override the need for proper testimony for the end.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if the sky is clear on the 30th night, the majority say continue fasting; Imam Muhammad says break.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The relied-upon position is that under cloud cover, all agree the fast ends after 30 days. In clear skies, the majority view prevails: the fast continues until sighting or two witnesses. Ibn al-Humam adds that if the start was accepted in clear skies, the fast does not end after 30 days even by agreement.
Al-Zayla'i says the most apparent is that under clouds it is permissible, otherwise not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولهم : جمع يقع العلم بخبرهم ، ويحكم العقل بعدم تواطيهم على الكذب . ( وبعد صوم " ثلاثين بقول عدلين حل الفطر"، وبقول عدل لا ) (۱) : أي إذا شهد واحد عدل بهلال رمضان ، وفي السَّماء علة ، فصاموا ثلاثين لا يحل الفطر نفعاً دنيوياً للعباد، فأشبه سائر حقوقهم، فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في حقوقهم، ولا كذلك هلال رمضان، فإنّه أمر ديني محض، وإنّما لا تشترط الدعوى ؛ لأنه ليس حق العبدِ تمحضاً ، بل فيه حق الله ، أيضا ، والدعوى إنّما هي في حقوق العباد الخالصة. [١]قوله : جمع يقع ... الخ ؛ ظاهر كلامه مشير إلى أن المراد به ما يبلغ عدد التواتر المفيد للعلم اليقيني، لكنّ الأمر ليس كذلك، بل المراد الجمعُ الذي يحصلُ بخبرهم غلبة الظن، وهو مفوّض إلى رأي الإمام من غير تقدير عدد، وهو الصحيح، والعالم الثقة في بلدة لا حاكم فيه قائم مقامه. [٣] قوله : حلّ الفطر؛ إن كانت السماء ليلة الحادية والثلاثين متغيمة، هذا بالاتفاق، وإن كانت مصحية ولم ير هلال شوال فكذلك على ما صححه في «الخلاصة»، و«البزازية»، وصحح عدمه في «مجموع النوازل»، واختار ابن الهمام () أنه إن قبلها في الصحو؛ أي في هلال رمضانَ وتم العدد لا يفطر، وإن قبلها في الغيم أفطروا. [٤] قوله : علة ؛ ؛ بكسر العين، وتشديد اللام ؛ أي مانع من الرؤية كالسحاب ؛ أي يكون يوم التاسع العشرين من شعبان غيم ونحوه، فلم تحصل رؤية الهلال لكل واحدٍ بل لواحد، فشهد به وقبل خبره، أما إن لم تكن علةً فلا يقبلُ فيه خبر الواحد. [١] قوله : لا يثبت بقول واحد ؛ ولو حكمنا بلزوم الواحد لزم ثبوته بقول واحد ؛ لكونه مبنياً على تمام العدد المبني على شهادة الواحد. [٢]قوله : خلافاً لمحمد الله ؛ ذكر بعضُهم أن خلاف محمد الله فيما إذا غم هلالُ الفطر، والمعتمد ما في «الذخيرة» و«المجتبى»، وغيرهما : إنّه يحلّ الفطر في الغيم اتفاقاً، وخلافُ محمد الله فيما إذا لم يغم، ولم ير ،الهلال، فعندهما: لا يحل الفطر، وعنده يحلّ، وذكر في «غاية البيان»: إنّ الأصح في صورة عدم الغيم قول محمد له، وقال الزيلعي : الأشبه إن غمّ حَلّ، وإلا لا. [٣]قوله : فإنّ الفطر ؛ حاصله : أنَّه لم يثبت الفطرُ في هذه الصورة قصداً، وإنما ثبت تبعاً ؛ لأنه لَمَّا حَكَمَ القاضي بقول الواحد في رمضانَ ووجب الصوم به ، وتم عدده ثبت الفطر تبعاً. [٤] قوله : وكم من شيء ... الخ ؛ كشهادة القابلة في النسب، فإنها تقبل ثم يفضي ذلك إلى استحقاق الميراث مع أن الميراث لا يثبت بشهادة المرأة الواحدة ابتداء. [0] قوله : في الأحكام المذكورة؛ فلا يثبتُ هلالُ ذي الحجة في الغيم إلا برجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، وفي الصحو لا بد من زيادة العدد بحيث تحصل غلبةُ الظَّنَّ.
Their saying: 'A group whose report produces knowledge, and reason judges the impossibility of them conspiring upon falsehood.' (And after fasting thirty days with the testimony of two just men, breaking the fast is permitted, and with the testimony of one just man it is not). That is: if one just witness testifies to the moon of Ramadan while there is an obstruction in the sky, and they fast thirty days, breaking the fast is not permitted because it is a worldly benefit for the servants, so it resembles other rights; thus the same conditions are required as in rights. Not so the moon of Ramadan, for it is a purely religious matter; and the requirement of a claim is not made because it is not purely a right of the servant, but rather it involves the right of Allah as well; the claim is only in pure rights of the servants. [1] His saying: 'a group whose report produces knowledge'... The apparent meaning of his words indicates that what is meant is the number that reaches tawatur which produces certain knowledge, but it is not so; rather what is meant is the group whose report produces overwhelming probability, and this is delegated to the Iman's opinion without specifying a number, and this is correct. The trustworthy scholar in a town where there is no judge acts in his place. [2] His saying: 'after fasting thirty days...' Means if two witness to the moon of Ramadan, and he judges the fast based on their testimony, and they fast thirty days, then after its completion it becomes permissible for them to break the fast, whether the moon of Shawwal is sighted or not, because the month does not exceed thirty, and Ramadan has been established by the legally valid testimony in the chapter of rulings. [3] His saying: 'breaking the fast is permitted.' If the sky on the night of the thirty-first is cloudy, this is by agreement. If it is clear and the moon of Shawwal is not sighted, then likewise according to what is verified in Al-Khulasa and Al-Bazzaziyya; and its negation is verified in Majmu' al-Nawazil. Ibn al-Humam chose that if he accepted it in clear skies (i.e., for the moon of Ramadan) and the number is completed, they do not break the fast; if he accepted it in cloudy skies, they break it. [4] His saying: 'obstruction' (illa) with a kasra on the 'ayn and tashdid on the lam, meaning a barrier to sighting like clouds. That is, if the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban is cloudy and like that, and no sighting occurs for everyone but only for one person, he testifies and his report is accepted. But if there is no obstruction, the report of a single person is not accepted. [1] His saying: 'it is not established by a single report.' If we were to rule by the obligation of the one, it would necessitate its establishment by a single report because it is based on completion of the number based on the testimony of one. [2] His saying: 'contrary to Muhammad.' Some mentioned that the disagreement of Muhammad is when the moon of Shawwal is hidden; and the relied upon position as in Al-Dhakhira and Al-Mujtaba and others is that breaking the fast in cloudy weather is by agreement. The disagreement of Muhammad is when it is not cloudy and the moon is not sighted; according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) breaking the fast is not permissible; according to him it is. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that the most correct in case of no clouds is the saying of Muhammad. Al-Zayla'i said: the most apparent is that if it is cloudy, it is permissible; otherwise no. [3] His saying: 'for breaking the fast...' The summary is that breaking the fast is not established intentionally in this case, but rather established by following, because when the judge ruled by the single report concerning Ramadan and fasting became obligatory by it, and its number is completed, breaking the fast is established by following. [4] His saying: 'and how many things...' Like the testimony of the midwife regarding lineage; it is accepted and then leads to entitlement to inheritance even though inheritance is not established by the testimony of a single woman initially. [0] His saying: 'in the previously mentioned rulings.' Thus the moon of Dhu al-Hijjah in cloudy skies is not established except by two men or a man and two women. In clear skies, an increased number is necessary such that overwhelming probability is obtained.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of moon sighting testimony for Ramadan and Shawwal. The author first clarifies that a 'group' producing knowledge means a number that yields overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) rather than certain knowledge (tawatur), and the Imam may decide the number. Then he explains that if two just witnesses testify to the crescent of Ramadan and the fast begins, after 30 days the fast ends even if the Shawwal crescent is not seen, because the month cannot exceed 30 days. There is a difference of opinion regarding a single witness: under cloud cover (ghaym), his testimony is accepted to start Ramadan, but not to end it according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad argues that if the start was established by one witness, the end is established implicitly by completion of 30 days, just as many things are established indirectly (e.g., a midwife's testimony leads to inheritance). However, the relied-upon position is that breaking the fast with a single witness is not allowed except in cloudy weather by agreement. The rules for Eid al-Adha are analogous to those for Eid al-Fitr: the crescent of Dhu al-Hijjah requires two men or a man and two women under clouds; in clear skies, a larger number is needed to overcome doubt.

Key Terms
جمع (jamm'): A group of witnesses whose report produces overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) of the moon sighting, not necessarily reaching tawatur.
عدل (adl): A just witness whose integrity ('adalah) is established and whose testimony is legally valid.
علة (illah (here meaning obstruction)): Any atmospheric obstruction preventing the moon's visibility, such as clouds or dust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when does the fast of Ramadan end if the sky is clear on the 30th night and no crescent is sighted?
A) It ends automatically after 30 days.
B) It continues until the crescent is sighted or 30 days from the start based on two witnesses.
C) It ends if the start was established by one witness.
D) It ends only if two witnesses testify to the crescent of Shawwal.

Key Takeaway
A single witness suffices for Ramadan only under cloud cover; ending the fast in clear skies requires either sighting or two witnesses, per the majority Hanafi position.

The Hanafi Dispute on One Witness for the Crescent of Eid
Sharh commentary on the rule for crescent sighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on accepting a single witness for the crescent of Eid al-Fitr in cloudy and clear weather, and explain the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
A single witness suffices to start fasting but not to end it — except by agreement when cloudy.

This passage from a sharh on al-Wiqayah delves into a precise fiqh dispute: when the sky is cloudy on the 29th of Ramadan, can the testimony of one trustworthy person be accepted to establish the crescent of Eid al-Fitr? The answer is not straightforward even within the Hanafi school. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that breaking the fast requires greater certainty, while Imam Muhammad allows it based on incidental evidence. The commentator reconciles the views, stating that the relied-upon fatwa follows ease in cloudy conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its analogy
Note that the passage begins with 'Eid al-Adha is like Eid al-Fitr' — meaning the same rule applies to both festivals. The key point is that breaking the fast (futur) is not established by a single person's testimony (khabar al-wahid).
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Find where the author states 'khilāfan li-Muḥammad' — this signals that Imam Muhammad disagrees with the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Understand the basis of his disagreement: that the end of fasting is incidental to its beginning, which was established by one witness.
3
Analyse the two scenarios: cloudy vs. clear
The passage distinguishes between cloudy (ghaym) and clear weather. In clouds, the relied-upon position (al-muʿtamad) is that there is agreement (ittifāqan) to accept one witness. In clear weather, the ikhtilaf remains: Muhammad accepts one witness, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf require more. Note the citation from Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Zayla'i.
4
Understand the incidental (tabaʿan) argument
Imam Muhammad's proof uses the principle that many things are established incidentally but not intentionally. The example of the midwife's testimony is given: a single woman's testimony establishes lineage, which then leads to inheritance — but inheritance alone would require more witnesses. Similarly, the completion of the month begins with one witness, and the end follows.
5
Apply the ruling to Dhu al-Hijjah
The passage concludes by extending the rule to the crescent of Dhu al-Hijjah (for Eid al-Adha): in clouds, two men or one man and two women; in clear weather, even more witnesses to achieve predominant probability (ghalabat al-ẓann).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأضحى كالفطر
لأنَّ الفطر لا يثبت بقول واحد خلافاً لمحمد الله ، فإنَّ الفطر يثبت عنده بتبعية الصوم، وكم من شيء يثبت ضمناً، ولا يثبت قصداً.
يكون يوم التاسع العشرين من شعبان غيم ونحوه، فلم تحصل رؤية الهلال لكل واحدٍ بل لواحد، فشهد به وقبل خبره، أما إن لم تكن علةً فلا يقبلُ فيه خبر الواحد.
قوله : لا يثبت بقول واحد ؛ ولو حكمنا بلزوم الواحد لزم ثبوته بقول واحد ؛ لكونه مبنياً على تمام العدد المبني على شهادة الواحد.
قوله : خلافاً لمحمد الله ؛ ذكر بعضُهم أن خلاف محمد الله فيما إذا غم هلالُ الفطر، والمعتمد ما في «الذخيرة» و«المجتبى»، وغيرهما : إنّه يحلّ الفطر في الغيم اتفاقاً، وخلافُ محمد الله فيما إذا لم يغم، ولم ير الهلال، فعندهما: لا يحل الفطر، وعنده يحلّ، وذكر في «غاية البيان»: إنّ الأصح في صورة عدم الغيم قول محمد له، وقال الزيلعي : الأشبه إن غمّ حَلّ، وإلا لا.
قوله : فإنّ الفطر ؛ حاصله : أنَّه لم يثبت الفطرُ في هذه الصورة قصداً، وإنما ثبت تبعاً ؛ لأنه لَمَّا حَكَمَ القاضي بقول الواحد في رمضانَ ووجب الصوم به ، وتم عدده ثبت الفطر تبعاً.
قوله : وكم من شيء ... الخ ؛ كشهادة القابلة في النسب، فإنها تقبل ثم يفضي ذلك إلى استحقاق الميراث مع أن الميراث لا يثبت بشهادة المرأة الواحدة ابتداء.
قوله : في الأحكام المذكورة؛ فلا يثبتُ هلالُ ذي الحجة في الغيم إلا برجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، وفي الصحو لا بد من زيادة العدد بحيث تحصل غلبةُ الظَّنِّ.
واجي
And Eid al-Adha is like Eid al-Fitr. Because breaking the fast is not established by a single statement, contrary to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, for breaking the fast is established in his view by following the fast. And many things are established incidentally but not intentionally. It is the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban with clouds and the like, so the sighting of the crescent was not obtained for everyone but for one person, so he testified and his report was accepted. As for if there is no cloud, then the report of a single person is not accepted. He said: 'It is not established by a single statement.' If we ruled by the necessity of the one, its establishment by a single statement would follow, because it is based on the completion of the number based on the testimony of one. He said: 'Contrary to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him.' Some mentioned that Muhammad's difference is when the crescent of Eid al-Fitr is obscured. The relied-upon position in al-Dhakhira and al-Mujtaba and others is that breaking the fast is permissible in clouds by agreement, and Muhammad's difference is when there is no cloud and the crescent was not seen. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), breaking is not permissible; according to him, it is permissible. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that the soundest in the case of no cloud is Muhammad's statement. Al-Zayla'i said: 'If it was cloudy, it is permissible; otherwise, no.' He said: 'So breaking the fast.' The summary: that breaking the fast in this scenario is not established intentionally, but rather it is established incidentally. Because when the judge ruled by the statement of one in Ramadan and fasting became obligatory by it, and its number was completed, breaking the fast was established incidentally. He said: 'And many things...' like the testimony of the midwife regarding lineage, for it is accepted, then it leads to entitlement to inheritance, whereas inheritance is not established by the testimony of a single woman initially. He said: 'In the aforementioned rulings.' So the crescent of Dhu al-Hijjah is not established in clouds except by two men or one man and two women. In clear weather, an increase in number is necessary such that predominant probability is obtained. And something [?].
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that 'Eid al-Adha is like Eid al-Fitr' regarding the establishment of the crescent moon. The author explains that the crescent for Eid al-Fitr (and by analogy Eid al-Adha) is not established by the testimony of a single witness, because breaking the fast (futur) is a separate ruling from fasting, and a single witness suffices for the obligation of fasting but not for its cessation. Imam Muhammad differs: he holds that if the sky is cloudy, the testimony of one witness for the crescent of Eid al-Fitr is accepted because it is incidental to the obligation of fasting. The commentator provides a detailed dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not accept one witness for breaking the fast even in clouds; Muhammad accepts in clouds, and in clear weather, there is disagreement. The relied-upon position is that in clouds, there is consensus on permissibility; Muhammad's difference is only when the sky is clear but no one sees the crescent—he accepts one witness while the others do not. The commentator then gives an analogy: just as a midwife's testimony (a single woman) is accepted for establishing lineage, which then leads to inheritance (though inheritance normally requires more witnesses), so too the breaking of the fast is established accidentally by the completion of the month based on one witness. For the crescent of Dhu al-Hijjah (for Eid al-Adha), the same rule applies: in clouds, two men or one man and two women are needed; in clear weather, even more witnesses are required for predominant probability.

Key Terms
الأضحى (al-adha): Eid al-Adha, the festival of sacrifice.
الفطر (al-fitr): Breaking the fast, specifically referring to the end of Ramadan (Eid al-Fitr).
الغيم (al-ghaym): Cloudy sky that prevents sighting of the crescent.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): Report from a single person, which in this context refers to testimony about the new moon.
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Incidental establishment — a ruling that follows as a consequence of another established ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (المعتمد) in al-Dhakhira and al-Mujtaba, what is the ruling on the testimony of a single witness for the crescent of Eid al-Fitr when the sky is cloudy?
A) It is not accepted; two witnesses are required.
B) It is accepted, and breaking the fast is permissible by agreement of all Hanafi imams.
C) It is accepted only if the witness is a woman.
D) It is accepted only if the witness is a judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on accepting one witness for the crescent of Eid is: in clouds, it is accepted by agreement; in clear weather, the majority requires more witnesses, but the soundest view allows one witness.

Acts Requiring Qada and Kaffarah: Intercourse, Eating, Drinking
Chapter on what necessitates qada and kaffarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the acts that require both qada and kaffarah when done intentionally during Ramadan fast, and explain the proof (hadith and analogy) that establishes this ruling.

Core Idea
Intentional intercourse, eating, drinking, and similar pleasures nullify the fast and require both qada and kaffarah like zihar.

This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the core Hanafi position on what breaks the fast and necessitates both making up the day (qada) and expiation (kaffarah). The ruling is derived from a clear hadith and extended by analogy to eating and drinking. We will explore the primary acts, the proof, and the extent of kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the acts
List the specific acts mentioned that require both qada and kaffarah: intercourse (penetration), being penetrated, eating or drinking food or medicine intentionally, and the case of cupping followed by intentional eating based on a mistaken belief that the fast was already broken.
Note that eating something that is neither food nor medicine does not require kaffarah, only qada.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) ordering a man who intentionally had intercourse in Ramadan to expiate like zihar. This is transmitted by the six major hadith collections.
The hadith is a command (amr) which indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The Prophet's command (أَمَرَ) directly makes kaffarah obligatory for intercourse. Then, by analogy (qiyas), eating and drinking are included because they share the effective cause (illa): intentional nullification of the fast and attainment of pleasure/lust.
The illa is 'ta'ammud ma'a al-ifsad wa husul al-ladhdha' (intentional nullification plus pleasure).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Within the Hanafi school, there is disagreement on whether kaffarah is required for smoking tobacco. The commentator argues it is like food/medicine, but other later scholars say only qada is needed. Also, eating non-food/non-medicine (e.g., a stone) does not trigger kaffarah.
The mufta bihi for smoking may be the more lenient view (qada only), but the strict opinion here is recorded.
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
Use the illa of 'intentional nullification + pleasure' to test new substances. For example, smoking tobacco, taking pleasure in food-like substances, or anything that provides similar gratification would fall under the ruling.
The commentator explicitly applies this to smoking tobacco (دخان التنباك).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب موجب الإفساد
من جامع ، أو جومع في أحد السبيلين، أو أكل أو شرب غذاء، أو دواء عمداً ، أو احتجم فظَنَّ أَنه فَطْرَه فأكل عمداً، قضى وكفر كالمظاهر
باب موجب الإفساد
بفتح الجيم : أي ما يوجبه الإفساد كالقضاء والكفارة.
من جامع، أو جومع في أحدِ السبيلين أو أكل، أو شرب غذاء، أو دواء" عمداً ، أو احتجم " فظَنَّ أنَّه فَطَّرَه فأكل عمداً ، قضى وكفر كالمظاهر) (٤١)
قوله : أو جومع ؛ في إطلاق الجملتين إشارة إلى أنه لا يشترط لوجوب الكفارة على الواطئ والموطوءة وفاعل اللواطة ومن فعل بها الإنزال، بل نفس الجماع، وهو غيبوبة الحَشَفَةِ كاف. والأصل ما ثبت عند الأئمة الستَّةِ وغيرهم : إنَّ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَ مَن جامع في رمضان متعمداً نهاراً أن يُكفِّرَ بمثل كفّارةِ الظهار المذكورة في القرآن في سورة المجادلة، وألحق به الأكل والشرب عمداً ؛ لكونه نظيره في الإفساد عمداً، وحصول اللذة وقضاء الشهوة، ولم يحكم بوجوب الكفارة في أكل ما ليس دواءً ولا غذاء.
قوله : غذاء أو دواء : أي من شأنه أن يتغذَّى به ويتداوى به، ويُلحق به ما فيه صلاح بدنِهِ وتلنُّذُهُ به كالتلذذ بالغذاء، وبه يعلم أنه يجب القضاء والكفَّارة على مَن شرب دخان التنباكِ في الصوم، وقد فصلتُ هذه المسألة في رسالتي : «زجرٍ أرباب الرّيانِ عن شرب الدخان»، وفي رسالتي : «ترويح الجنان بتشريح حكم شرب الدخان».
قوله : أو احتجم ؛ أي استعمل الحجامة، وهذا ذكر اتفاقي، والغرض أنه فعل فعلاً لا يظن الفطر به كالحجامة والفصد ونحو ذلك، فإن من المعلوم أن الصوم لا يفسد إلا بما دخل لا بما خرج إلا ما سيأتي ذكره ، وهو الإنزالُ والقيء، فظنَّ بحماقته أنه فسد صومه فأكل أو شرب أو جامع عمدا.
(٤) قوله : كالمظاهر؛ أي الذي يُشبه زوجتَهُ أو عضواً منها بمحرمه أو جزئه :
(۱) المظاهر : وهو من يشبه ما يضاف إلى الطلاق من المنكوحة بما يحرم النظر إليه من عضو محرمه نسباً أو رضاعاً. ينظر: «الغرر»(۱ : ۳۹۳).
Chapter on what necessitates nullification. Whoever has intercourse, or is penetrated in one of the two passages, or eats or drinks intentionally food or medicine, or uses cupping and then thinks that it broke his fast and so eats intentionally, he must make up and expiate like the one who makes zihar. Chapter on what necessitates nullification: with a fatha on the jim, meaning what nullification obligates like qada and kaffarah. Whoever has intercourse, or is penetrated in one of the two passages, or eats, or drinks food or medicine intentionally, or uses cupping and then thinks that it broke his fast and so eats intentionally, he must make up and expiate like the one who makes zihar. His statement: 'or is penetrated' – in the absolute mention of the two sentences is an indication that the necessity of expiation is not conditional on the male ejaculator or on the penetrated female or the one who commits sodomy and the one on whom it is done, but rather the act of intercourse itself, which is the disappearance of the glans, is sufficient. The foundation is that which is established by the six imams and others: the Prophet, peace be upon him, ordered the one who had intercourse in Ramadan intentionally during the day to expiate with an expiation like that of zihar mentioned in the Qur'an in Surat al-Mujadilah, and he attached to it eating and drinking intentionally because it is similar in intentional nullification, attainment of pleasure, and fulfillment of desire. And he did not rule the obligation of expiation for eating what is neither food nor medicine. His statement: 'food or medicine' – that which is nourished or treated with, and attached to it is that which benefits his body and by which he takes pleasure like the pleasure of food. And by this it is known that qada and kaffarah are obligatory on one who smokes tobacco during fasting, and I have detailed this issue in my treatise 'Zajr arbab al-riyan an shurb al-dukhan' and in my treatise 'Tarwih al-jinan bi-tashrih hukm shurb al-dukhan'. His statement: 'or uses cupping' – meaning he used hijama, and this is an incidental mention. The purpose is that he performs an act that is not thought to break the fast, like cupping, phlebotomy, and the like, for it is known that fasting is only nullified by what enters, not by what exits except for what will be mentioned later, i.e., seminal emission and vomiting. So he foolishly thought his fast was broken and ate, drank, or had intercourse intentionally. His statement: 'like the one who makes zihar' – that is, one who likens his wife or a part of her to a mahram or a part of a mahram. (1) Al-Muzahir: he who likens what is added to divorce of a wife to what is unlawful to look at from the body of a mahram by lineage or breastfeeding. See al-Ghurur (1:393).
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is the chapter heading and initial commentary on 'What Necessitates Nullification' (موجب الإفساد) of the fast, specifically regarding qada (making up) and kaffarah (expiation). The ruling: Whoever intentionally has intercourse (penetration of the glans) in one of the two passages (front or back), or is penetrated (by another), or eats or drinks food or medicine intentionally, or uses cupping (hijama) and then mistakenly thinks that this act broke his fast and then intentionally eats, drinks, or has intercourse, must both make up that day and perform the expiation of zihar (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor). The commentator explains that the kaffarah applies equally to the penetrator and the one penetrated, and is not conditional on ejaculation—mere disappearance of the glans suffices. The proof cited: the hadith from the six imams that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) ordered expiation for intentional intercourse in Ramadan, and by analogy, eating and drinking intentionally are included because they also involve intentional nullification and attainment of pleasure. However, eating something that is neither food nor medicine (e.g., a stone) does not require kaffarah, only qada. On the issue of smoking tobacco, the commentator asserts it requires both qada and kaffarah because it resembles food/medicine in providing pleasure and benefit (صلاح بدن). He references his own treatises. For cupping, the ruling is that it does not break the fast (since nothing enters), but if the person ignorantly thinks it does and then intentionally eats, kaffarah is still required because the act was a deliberate nullification after assuming the fast was already broken.

Key Terms
موجب الإفساد (mujib al-ifsad): What necessitates nullification of the fast, i.e., the ruling that follows from the nullification (qada and kaffarah).
كالمظاهر (ka al-muzahir): Like the one who performs zihar, i.e., the expiation is the same as that for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.
غيبوبة الحشفة (ghaybat al-hashafah): Disappearance of the glans of the penis, which is the minimal criterion for intercourse to nullify the fast and trigger kaffarah.
دخان التنباك (dukhan al-tinbak): Tobacco smoke, which the commentator argues is like food/medicine in providing pleasure and thus requires qada and kaffarah if consumed intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, which of the following acts requires both qada and kaffarah?
A) Eating a small stone intentionally.
B) Smoking tobacco intentionally during the fast.
C) Vomiting intentionally without any other act.
D) Swallowing water after rinsing the mouth accidentally.

Key Takeaway
Intentional acts that nullify the fast with pleasure, such as intercourse, eating, drinking, and similar substances, obligate both qada and kaffarah in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's command and analogy.

Acts Requiring Qada' and Kaffarah in Ramadan
Listing acts that break the fast and require both makeup and expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the acts that break the fast and require both qada and kaffarah according to the Hanafi school, and explain the proof from the Sunnah and qiyas.

Core Idea
Intentionally breaking the Ramadan fast by intercourse or eating/drinking triggers the same expiation as zihar.

This lesson focuses on a key ruling from the Hanafi school regarding actions that invalidate the Ramadan fast. The matn and commentary list specific acts—intercourse (active and passive), eating, drinking, and a special case involving cupping—that obligate not only makeup (qada) but also expiation (kaffarah). The proof is a direct command from the Prophet (PBUH) and an analogy (qiyas) that extends the ruling to similar acts. Understanding this passage is essential for correctly applying the consequences of deliberate fast-breaking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts listed
Read the matn to find the acts that require both qada and kaffarah: intentional intercourse (active and passive), intentional eating/drinking of food or medicine, and the case of cupping followed by intentional eating.
The text uses two forms (جامع and جومع) to include both active and passive partners.
2
Recognize the inclusive scope of intercourse
The commentary explains that 'السبيلين' (both passages) are included, and that the mere act of union (ghaybah al-hashafah) is sufficient, regardless of desire or enjoyment.
This covers vaginal and anal intercourse, for both the one who performs and the one upon whom it is performed.
3
Examine the primary proof (hadith)
The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) commanded the man who deliberately had intercourse in Ramadan to expiate with the expiation of zihar. The Hanafi principle that 'amr' indicates obligation (wujub) is applied here.
The hadith is transmitted by the six Imams (Bukhari, Muslim, etc.), but it is ahad, giving it zanni thubut.
4
Understand the analogy to eating/drinking
Eating and drinking are annexed (mulhiq) to intercourse by qiyas because they share the same illa: intentional invalidation of the fast and attainment of pleasure or fulfillment of desire.
The text explicitly states that the ruling is extended to acts that provide benefit to the body and pleasure, similar to food.
5
Define the conditions of food/medicine
The commentary restricts 'food or medicine' to what is customarily used for nourishment or treatment. Things that are neither (e.g., inedible objects) do not require kaffarah, though qada may still be necessary.
This sets a boundary for the analogy: only items that serve a similar purpose as food/drink are included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من جامع، أو جومع في أحد السبيلين، أو أكل أو شرب غذاء، أو دواء عمداً ، أو احتجم فظن أنه فطره فأكل عمداً، قضى وكفر كالمظاهر. قوله : أو جومع ؛ في إطلاق الجملتين إشارة إلى أنه لا يشترط لوجوب الكفارة على الواطئ والموطوءة وفاعل اللواطة ومن فعل بها الإنزال، بل نفس الجماع، وهو غيبوبة الحشفة كاف. والأصل ما ثبت عند الأئمة الستة وغيرهم : إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أمر من جامع في رمضان متعمداً نهاراً أن يكفر بمثل كفارة الظهار المذكورة في القرآن في سورة المجادلة، وألحق به الأكل والشرب عمداً ؛ لكونه نظيره في الإفساد عمداً، وحصول اللذة وقضاء الشهوة، ولم يحكم بوجوب الكفارة في أكل ما ليس دواءً ولا غذاء. قوله : غذاء أو دواء : أي من شأنه أن يتغذى به ويتداوى به، ويلحق به ما فيه صلاح بدنه وتلذذه به كالتلذذ بالغذاء.
[From the matn:] Whoever engages in sexual intercourse, or has intercourse performed upon him in one of the two passages, or eats or drinks food or medicine intentionally, or uses cupping and then thinks that it broke his fast and so eats intentionally, must make up (the fast) and expiate like the one who declares zihar. [From the commentary:] His statement: 'or has intercourse performed upon him' – in the mention of both phrases is an indication that for the obligation of expiation upon the one who has intercourse and the one with whom intercourse is performed, the one who commits sodomy and the one upon whom it is committed, and the one who causes emission, it is not required that there be actual desire; rather, the mere act of intercourse, which is the disappearance of the glans, is sufficient. The basis is what is established by the six Imams and others: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded the one who deliberately had intercourse during the day in Ramadan to expiate with an expiation like the expiation of zihar mentioned in the Quran in Surah al-Mujadalah. And eating and drinking intentionally were annexed to it because they are similar in intentional invalidation and attaining pleasure and fulfillment of desire. And he did not rule that expiation is obligatory for eating something that is neither food nor medicine. His statement: 'food or medicine' – meaning that which is customarily used for nourishment or treatment, and to it is annexed whatever benefits the body and brings pleasure as with food.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its proof from the Sunnah. The matn states that intentional sexual intercourse (in any form, whether one performs it or has it performed), eating or drinking food or medicine, and the case where one uses cupping and then mistakenly thinks his fast is broken and so eats intentionally — all these require both qada' and kaffarah. The kaffarah is the same as that of zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people. The commentary explains that the mention of 'جامع' and 'جومع' indicates that the ruling applies to both the active and passive partner; the condition for kaffarah is simply the act itself, not necessarily enjoyment or desire. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) commanding the man who broke his fast by intercourse to perform the kaffarah of zihar, and by analogy, eating and drinking intentionally are included because they also invalidate the fast and involve pleasure. The commentary also clarifies that 'food or medicine' means items customarily consumed as nourishment or treatment, and anything that provides similar benefit or pleasure is annexed. This is based on the Hanafi principle of qiyas (analogy) with the original case.

Key Terms
جومع (juumi'a): He who has intercourse performed upon him, i.e., the passive partner in intercourse.
السبيلين (al-sabīlayn): The two passages – the front (vagina/penis) and the back (anus).
مثل كفارة الظهار (mithlu kaffārati al-ẓihār): The expiation like that of zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Eating or drinking unintentionally
B) Using cupping and then eating intentionally
C) Being coerced into eating
D) Using a nasal spray

Key Takeaway
Intentional acts of invalidation (intercourse, eating, drinking) during Ramadan fast require both qada and kaffarah of zihar, based on the hadith and qiyas.

Kaffarah Specific to Ramadan Fast
Scope of kaffarah in Ramadan fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which acts of fast-breaking require kaffarah and which require only qada', based on the Hanafi school's ruling.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is wajib only for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast—other cases need only qada'.

Many assume any fast-breaking act demands expiation, but the Hanafi school restricts kaffarah to deliberate invalidation of the Ramadan fast. This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah outlines the scope and lists exceptions where only makeup (qada') is owed. Understanding this distinction prevents incorrect application of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The text begins: 'kaffarah is by invalidating the fast of Ramadan only.' This establishes that kaffarah is exclusive to the Ramadan fast, not other types of fasting.
The ruling is based on specific hadith, not general analogy.
2
Recognize exceptions requiring only qada'
The text lists: breaking fast by mistake (khaṭa'), under coercion, using an enema, nasal spray, or ear drops. For all these, only qada' is required.
The commentary confirms: 'qada' only' is the result for these conditions.
3
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that kaffarah is not extended by qiyas (analogy) because the textual evidence (hadith) is specific to deliberate acts in Ramadan.
This prevents applying kaffarah to other fasts or accidental breaks.
4
Distinguish between mistake and forgetfulness
Khaṭa' (mistake) means being mindful of the fast but unintentionally breaking it (e.g., water entering throat while rinsing). If not mindful, it is nisyān (forgetfulness), which also requires only qada'.
Forgetfulness is not covered by the term 'khaṭa'' in the passage.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Given a scenario, determine if the fast-breaking was deliberate and during Ramadan. If yes, kaffarah is wajib; otherwise, only qada'.
This step cements the hierarchical rule.

Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that clarifies the scope of kaffarah. The text begins by stating that kaffarah (expiation) is only for invalidating the fast of Ramadan, not for other fasts. It then lists situations where the fast is broken but only qada' is required, not kaffarah: breaking the fast by mistake (e.g., water going down the throat while rinsing), under coercion (someone forces you to eat/drink), using an enema, using a nasal spray, or putting drops in the ear. The commentary explains that the word 'لا غير' (only) means that kaffarah is not required for invalidating supererogatory (nafl) fasts, sunnah fasts, wajib fasts, or makeup fasts of Ramadan, nor for breaking the fast of Ramadan by mistake, coercion, or forgetfulness. The reason is that the textual evidence (hadith) specifically addresses the case of deliberately breaking the Ramadan fast, and kaffarah is not established by qiyas (analogy) to be extended to other cases. The commentary also parses the condition 'إن أفطر خطأ...' and states that the result is 'قضى فقط' (only qada'). It defines 'خطأ' (mistake) as being mindful of the fast but breaking it without intending to, such as water entering the throat while rinsing; if one was not mindful, it is forgetfulness (nisyan), not mistake. 'مكرهاً' means being coerced by another person. 'احتقن' means using an enema. 'أقطر' means putting oil or medicine into the ear. All these cases require only qada' (makeup) of the fast, not kaffarah.

Key Terms
خطأ (khaṭa'): Mistake: being mindful of the fast but accidentally breaking it without intention, e.g., water entering throat while rinsing.
قسى فقط (qaḍá faqaṭ): Only makeup (qada') is required, no expiation.

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah is wajib only for deliberately invalidating a Ramadan fast; all other invalidations require only qada'.

Kaffarah Only for Invalidating Ramadan Fast Intentionally
Establishes scope of kaffarah and lists exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which kaffarah is wajib and distinguish cases that require only qada.

Core Idea
Kaffarah is wajib only for intentionally invalidating a Ramadan fast; all other invalidations require only qada.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the scope of kaffarah, clarifying that it applies exclusively to intentional violation of Ramadan fasting. The commentator expands on exceptions and intra-Hanafi differences, particularly regarding the case of induced vomiting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of kaffarah
Determine that kaffarah is wajib only for intentionally invalidating a Ramadan fast. Note that the text explicitly says 'لا غير' (only).
This is the core ruling.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is a specific text (nas) that came regarding Ramadan only. The obligation is not established by qiyas, so it does not extend to other fasts.
Dalil is naqli, not qiyasi.
3
List cases requiring only qada
Identify the many exceptions: mistake, compulsion, enemas, snuff, ear drops, deep wounds, swallowing non-food, vomiting (with ikhtilaf), eating suhur after dawn thinking it was still night, etc.
All these involve shubha (doubt), so only qada is required.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on vomiting
For vomiting that does not fill the mouth: Muhammad holds it invalidates the fast, Abu Yusuf does not. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf.
This shows the importance of effective exit (khuruj hukman).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(أو أقطر في أُذُنِه كانت علي كظهر أمي، وسيأتي تفصيله في كتاب النكاح. [1] قوله : مثل كفارة الظهار ؛ وهي تحرير رقبة فإن لم يستطع فصيام شهرين متتابعين، فإن لم يستطع فإطعام ستين مسكينا. [٢]قوله : لا غير؛ فلا تجب بإفسادِ صوم النفل والسنة والواجب وقضاء رمضان ، رمضان خطأ أو إكراها أو نسياناً ؛ لأنَّ النَّص الوارد في هذا الباب إنما ولا بإفساد صوم ورد في أداء رمضان لا في غيره، وليس وجوبها قياساً حتى يتعدى إلى غيره. [٣] قوله : إن أفطر؛ هذا مع ما عطف عليه شرط ، وجزاؤه قوله: فيما يأتي «قضى فقط». 41 ] قوله : أن يكون ؛ فإن لم يكن ذاكراً له فهو نسيان لا خطأ. [0] قوله : قصد ؛ أي قصد الإفطار، فإنَّ قصده كان عمداً. [٦] قوله : أو مكرهاً ؛ بصيغة المفعول أي الكراهية، أي أكرهه إنسان على الأكل أو الشرب أو الجماع ففعل. [۷] قوله : أو احتقن ؛ أي استعمل الحقنة، وأوصل الدواء بها من الدبر إلى جوفه. (۸) قوله : أو أقطر؛ من الإقطار: أي صب في إذنِهِ دهناً ونحوه مما فيه صلاح البدن، ولو أقطر الماء أو أدخلَهُ في نفسه لا يفسد الصوم. كذا في «الهداية). [١]قوله : حصاة ، بالفتح : سنگريزه ، وكذا كلُّ ما لا يأكلُهُ الإنسانُ أو يستقذره كأوراق الأشجار. [٢] قوله : استقاء ؛ أي أخرج القيء عمداً وقد ملأ فمه به، فإن لم يكن ملأ الفم فهو مفسد عند محمد ه ؛ لإطلاق الحديث الذي سيأتي ذكره، وعند أبي يوسف : لا يفسد ؛ لعدم الخروج حكماً. كذا في (الهداية) [٣]قوله : أو تسيّر ؛ يعني أكل السَّحْرَ بظنّ أنَّ اللَّيلَ باق، ثمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّ الصُّبحَ طلع ، وكذا لو أفطر ظانَّا أَنَّ الشَّمس غربت، فإذا هي لم تغرب. (٤) قوله : أو أصبح ؛ أي لم ينو من الليل، وكان يمكن له أن ينوي من النهار لكنه مع الإمساك، فيجب القضاء لعدم العبادة بفقد النيَّة. ينظر : (مجمع الأنهر» (١) : ٢٤٤). (٤) فيجب القضاء عليه ولا كفارة سواء كان قبل الزوال أو بعده ؛ لما حصل من الشبهة، وعندهما تجب الكفارة. ينظر : «مجمع الأنهر» (١) : ٢٤٤). (٥) «الهداية» (۱ : ۱۲۵). (٦) (الهداية» (۲) : ٣٣٥).
It (kaffarah) is only for invalidating the fast of Ramadan, and if one breaks the fast mistakenly or under compulsion, or used an enema, or used snuff, or put drops in his ear — its kaffarah is like the kaffarah of dhihar. (He said: meaning expiation) (for invalidating the fast of Ramadan only) meaning invalidating the performance of Ramadan intentionally. (And if he broke the fast mistakenly) — this is when he remembers the fast but breaks it without a valid excuse intentionally, such as when he rinses his mouth and water enters his throat, or under compulsion, or used an enema, or used snuff — meaning he poured medicine into his nose and it reached his nasal passage. (Or put drops in his ear) — it is like saying to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother', and its detail will come in the Book of Marriage. [1] His saying: similar to the kaffarah of dhihar — which is freeing a slave, and if unable then fasting two consecutive months, and if unable then feeding sixty poor people. [2] His saying: only — so it is not obligatory for invalidating a supererogatory fast, or a sunnah fast, or a required fast, or a makeup of Ramadan, or a Ramadan fast broken mistakenly or under compulsion or forgetfully; because the text that came on this subject is only about performing Ramadan, not others, and its obligation is not by analogy such that it extends to others. [3] His saying: if he breaks — this along with what is coordinated with it is a condition, and its result is his saying later 'he only makes up'. [4] His saying: such that he is — if he does not remember it then it is forgetfulness, not mistake. [5] His saying: intentionally — meaning he intended to break the fast, because his intent was deliberate. [6] His saying: or under compulsion — in the passive form meaning coercion, i.e., a person forced him to eat or drink or have intercourse, and he did it. [7] His saying: or used an enema — meaning he used an enema and introduced medicine through the anus into his stomach. (8) His saying: or put drops — from iqtar: i.e., he poured oil or similar into his ear which is beneficial for the body, and if he poured water or inserted it into himself it does not invalidate the fast. This is in al-Hidayah. [1] His saying: a pebble — with fatha: a small stone, and similarly everything that a human does not eat or finds disgusting, like tree leaves. [2] His saying: he induced vomiting — meaning he brought out vomit intentionally and it filled his mouth; if it did not fill the mouth, it is an invalidator according to Muhammad, due to the general nature of the hadith that will be mentioned, and according to Abu Yusuf: it does not invalidate, due to lack of effective exit. This is in al-Hidayah. [3] His saying: or ate suhur — meaning he ate the pre-dawn meal thinking the night remained, then he learned that dawn had risen, and similarly if he broke the fast thinking the sun had set, when it had not. (4) His saying: or he woke up — meaning he did not intend from the night, and it was possible for him to intend from the daytime, but he [remained] with abstention, so qada becomes obligatory due to the absence of worship from lack of intention. See: Majma' al-Anhur (1:244). (4) So qada is obligatory on him and no kaffarah, whether before midday or after, because of the doubt (shubha) that occurred; according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] kaffarah is obligatory. See: Majma' al-Anhur (1:244). (5) al-Hidayah (1:125). (6) al-Hidayah (2:335).
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that kaffarah (expiation) is only obligated for intentionally invalidating a Ramadan fast. The commentator expands on the text, clarifying that the kaffarah is the same as that for zihar (a pre-Islamic form of divorce), which is specified in the Quran (Surah al-Mujadilah: 3-4): freeing a slave, or fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people. The commentator then explains that kaffarah is not required for invalidating supererogatory, sunnah, obligatory, or makeup fasts, nor for Ramadan fasts broken accidentally, under compulsion, or forgetfully. The reason is that the proof (nas) is specific to the Ramadan fast, and it is not extended by analogy. The passage then lists cases where only qada (makeup) is required: breaking the fast mistakenly (like water entering the throat during rinsing), under compulsion, using an enema, using snuff, putting oil in the ear, treating a deep wound (ja'ifah) or skull fracture (ammah) that reaches the stomach or brain, swallowing a pebble or iron, inducing vomiting (with a notable intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if the vomit does not fill the mouth, Muhammad considers it invalidating, while Abu Yusuf does not), eating suhur thinking it was still night, breaking the fast thinking the sun set when it hadn't, eating forgetfully then intentionally thinking the fast was broken, intercourse with a sleeping woman, not having intention for the entire month while abstaining, and waking up without intention and eating. In all these cases, only qada is obligatory; kaffarah is waived due to shubha (doubt). The commentator notes a disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa (the text's position), no kaffarah; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), kaffarah is required in some cases (like waking up without intention and eating). The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as stated in the text.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for intentionally invalidating a Ramadan fast, consisting of freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor people.
خطأ (khata'): Mistake: when one remembers the fast but breaks it unintentionally, e.g., water entering throat while rinsing.
استقاء (istiqa'): Intentional induction of vomiting; if it fills the mouth, it invalidates the fast; otherwise, there is ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases is kaffarah (expiation) obligatory according to the Hanafi school?
A) Breaking a supererogatory fast intentionally
B) Eating forgetfully during Ramadan
C) Intentionally invalidating the Ramadan fast with no excuse
D) Breaking the fast of Ramadan under compulsion

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah is wajib only when a Ramadan fast is intentionally invalidated without any shubha; all other invalidations require only qada.

Actions Requiring Qada But Not Kaffarah During Fasting
Enumeration of actions requiring only makeup during fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the actions that require only qada, explain the principle that fast is broken by what enters, and distinguish between cases requiring qada versus kaffarah.

Core Idea
Qada is required when a fast-breaking substance enters the body, but kaffarah needs full intentional transgression.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from Al-Wiqayah enumerating several actions that break the fast but do not require kaffarah. Understanding this distinction is key to knowing the consequences of different types of violations. The Hanafi school's position is based on the statement of Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ali that breaking the fast is by what enters, not what exits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Overall Ruling
The passage states that for a list of actions during fasting, only qada (makeup) is required, not kaffarah (expiation). Understand that this is a ruling of the Hanafi school.
Kaffarah is a heavier penalty, only for intentional violation with full transgression.
2
Categorize the Listed Actions
Group the actions: forgetful (eating, drinking, intercourse), involuntary (wet dream, being overcome by vomiting, dust entering), improper but not intentional (applying oil, kissing, backbiting, waking in janabah).
Some actions like backbiting are moral sins but still break the fast per this text.
3
Analyze the Proof (Dalil)
The sharh cites the saying of Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ali: 'Breaking the fast is by what enters, not what exits.' This principle indicates that any substance entering the body via a natural passage breaks the fast, even if unintentional.
The narration is a Qawl Sahabi, considered strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
4
Explain Why Kaffarah is Absent
Kaffarah depends on 'completeness of the violation' (takamil al-jinaayah). These cases lack either intent (forgetfulness) or full control (involuntary), so kaffarah is not wajib.
The sharh explicitly says: 'wa idh laysa fa-laysa' – since it is not (complete violation), it is not (required).
5
Note the Exception for Reminded Forgetful Eater
If a forgetful eater is reminded but persists, his fast becomes invalid (because now he knows) but still no kaffarah, as per al-Tatarkhaniyyah.
This shows that the obligation of qada remains, but kaffarah never applies when the act started forgetfully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قضى فقط ، ولو أكل أو شرب أو جامع ناسياً أو نام فاحتلم ، أو نظر إلى امرأته فأنزل ، أو ادهن ، أو اكتحل ، أو قبل ، أو اغتاب ، أو غلبه القيء، أو تقياً قليلاً أو أصبح جنباً ، أو صب في إحليله دهن، أو في أذنه ماء، أو دخل غبار، أو دخان ، أو ذباب في حلقه قضى فقط ) قوله : قضى فقط ; أما وجوب القضاء في هذه الصور فلوصول مفطر إلى داخل جوفٍ أو دماغ من أي سبيل كان، وقد قال ابن عباس وابن مسعودٍ وعلي : إن الفطر مما دخل وليس مما خرج ) ، أخرجه البيهقي وابن أبي شيبة وعبد الرزاق، ورواه أبو يعلى الموصلي مرفوعاً بسند ضعيف، وأما عدم الكفارة فلان وجوبها عند تكامل الجناية، وإذ ليس فليس. قوله : ناسياً ; إلا أن يأكل ناسياً فذكرَهُ رجلٌ أنك صائم فلم يتذكر ولم يتركِ الأكل فحينئذ يفسد صومه لأن خبر الواحد مقبول في الديانات، ولا كفارة. كذا في التاتارخانية. قوله : ادهن ; أي استعمل الدهن في شعر الرأس أو اللحية. قوله : أو اغتاب ; من الغيبة بالكسر : هو ذكر إنسان حال غيبته بما فيه بحيث لو سمعه لكرهه تحقيراً له، فإن ذكره بما ليس فيه فهو بهتان. قوله : أصبح ; أي طلع الصبح الصادق وهو جنب بوطء أو احتلام. (۱) ادَّهَن : أي دَهَنَ رَأْسَهُ أو شَارِبَهُ إذا طَلاهُ بِالدُّهْن ، وادَّهَنَ على افْتَعَلَ إِذَا تَوَلَّى ذلك من نفسِهِ من غير ذكر المفعول ، فقوله ادْهَنَ شَارِبَهُ خَطَقٌ. ينظر : «المغرب»(ص٦٨). (۲) في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (۲) : (۳۰۸) ، و (سنن البيهقي الكبير» (٤ : ٢٦١)، وغيرها. (۳) سواء ذكره بنقص في بدنه أو نسبه أو خلقه أو فعله. ينظر : «إحياء علوم الدين»(۳: ١٥٢).
Only qada (makeup) is required. And if one ate or drank or had intercourse forgetfully, or slept and had a wet dream, or looked at his wife and emitted semen, or applied oil, or applied kohl, or kissed, or backbit, or was overcome by vomiting, or vomited a little, or woke up in a state of janabah, or oil was poured into his urethra, or water into his ear, or dust or smoke or a fly entered his throat, then only qada (is required). He said: 'Only qada' - as for the obligation of qada in these cases, it is because a fast-breaking substance reached the interior of the stomach or brain from any path, and Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ali said: 'Breaking the fast is by what enters, not by what exits.' This was narrated by al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Shaybah, and Abd al-Razzaq, and Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili narrated it as a marfu' hadith with a weak chain. As for the absence of kaffarah, it is because its obligation depends on the completeness of the violation, and here it is not. He said: 'Forgetfully' - unless one eats forgetfully and a man reminds him that he is fasting, but he does not remember and does not stop eating, then his fast becomes invalid because the report of a single narrator is accepted in religious matters, and there is no kaffarah. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. He said: 'Applied oil' meaning he used oil on the hair of the head or beard. He said: 'Or backbit' - backbiting is mentioning a person in his absence with something that is in him such that if he heard it he would dislike it, as a belittlement. If he mentions something that is not in him, it is slander. He said: 'Became' meaning the true dawn rose while he was in a state of janabah due to intercourse or a wet dream.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Wiqayah, expanded by the sharh. The ruling: for a list of actions during fasting, only qada (makeup) is required, not kaffarah (expiation). The actions include eating, drinking, intercourse forgetfully; having a wet dream; looking at one's wife and emitting semen; applying oil or kohl; kissing; backbiting; being overcome by vomiting or vomiting a little; waking up in janabah; oil entering the urethra; water entering the ear; dust, smoke, or a fly entering the throat. The sharh explains that qada is wajib because a fast-breaking substance reaches the internal cavity (jawf or dimagh) from any pathway. It cites a saying of Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ali that the fast is broken by what enters, not what exits. The absence of kaffarah is because kaffarah requires complete transgression (jinaayah), which is not present in these cases due to forgetfulness, lack of intent, or minimal input. The sharh further clarifies: if a forgetful eater is reminded but persists, his fast is invalidated (since the reminder makes him aware), but still no kaffarah. It defines 'adehana' as applying oil to hair, 'ightabah' as backbiting, and 'asbaha' as waking at dawn in janabah. Lexical notes on the verb 'iddahana' are included.

Key Terms
ناسياً (naasiyan): Forgetfully, i.e., not remembering that one is fasting while performing an action that would otherwise break the fast.
اغتاب (ightaaba): Backbiting: mentioning a person in his absence with something he dislikes that is true about him, with the intent of belittlement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does backbiting during fasting require qada but not kaffarah according to the passage?
A) Because backbiting does not involve physical entry of a substance.
B) Because backbiting is a sin but not a fast-breaking act, so no qada is needed.
C) Because the passage includes backbiting in the list, and since it is an intentional act, kaffarah should be required.
D) The passage does not provide a specific reason, but it is included under the general principle that any act that reaches the stomach breaks the fast.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any substance entering the body via a natural passage breaks the fast and requires qada, but kaffarah is only for intentional, deliberate violations.

Actions That Do Not Break the Fast
Clarification that forgetful eating, wet dreams, etc. do not break the fast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetful eating, wet dreams, and injections during fasting, and identify the proofs for each.

Core Idea
Forgetful acts, wet dreams, and injections do not break the fast because they are not intentional or do not reach the stomach via usual openings.

This lesson examines specific actions that, despite occurring during a fast, do not invalidate it. We will explore the proofs from hadith and the conditions that define what constitutes a fast-breaker. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts ruled as non-invalidating
List the specific actions mentioned: forgetful eating/drinking, forgetful intercourse, wet dreams, subcutaneous injections.
These are distinct from intentional acts or acts that reach the stomach through normal pathways.
2
Examine the primary proof for forgetful eating
Analyze the hadith of the man who ate forgetfully; the Prophet told him to complete his fast. Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the command indicates the fast remains valid.
This hadith is narrated by the six major collectors and others.
3
Examine the proof for wet dreams
The hadith 'Three things do not break the fast' includes wet dreams. Though the chain is weak, it is supported by consensus of most imams.
The Hanafi school relies on the strength of the consensus (ijma) to accept this ruling.
4
Apply the condition for injections
The fatwa of Muhammad Bakheet explains that for something to break the fast, it must reach the stomach through the usual openings. Subcutaneous injections do not meet this condition.
This ruling is based on the principle that pores are not considered normal pathways.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يفطر [١]قوله : لم يفطر; أي لم يبطل صومُهُ في هذه الصورة ما في الأكل والشرب ناسيا، فالقياس وإن كان يقتضي فيها ، والصومُ كما في صورة الخطأ إلا أنه ترك ذلك، بما روى أنَّ رجلاً أكل وشرب ناسياً في الصوم فقال له رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «تم على صومك، فإنما أطعمك الله وسقاك ) ، أخرجَهُ الأئمةُ السِّتَّةُ والدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ وابنُ حَبَّانَ وغيرهم، بألفاظ متقاربة. وإذا ثبت هذا في الأكل والشرب ثبت في الجماع ناسياً؛ لأنه مثله، وليس في حكم الناسي المخطئ والمكره حتى يُلحق به في حكم، فيفسد صومها. وأما في صورة الاحتلام ; فلحديث: «ثلاث لا يفطرنَ الصَّائم : الحجامة، والقيء، والاحتلام ) ، أخرجه الترمذي بسند ضعيف، وتأيد ذلك بإجماع أكثر الأئمة. (1) أما حكم الاحتقان في العضدين أو غيره ، فقد أفتى الشيخ العلامة محمد بخيت : إن شرط المفطر أن يصل إلى الجوف وان يستقر فيه والمراد بذلك أن يدخل إلى الجوف ولا يكون طرفه خارج الجوف ولا متصلا بشيء خارج عن الجوف وأن يكون الوصول إلى الجوف من المنافذ المعتادة ; لأن المسام ونحوها من المنافذ التي لم تجر العادة بأن يصل منها شيء إلى الجوف، ومن ذلك يعلم أن الاحتقان بالحقن المعروف الآن عملها تحت الجلد سواء كان ذلك في العضدين أو الفخذين أو رأس الإليتين أو في أي موضع من ظاهر البدن غير مفسد للصوم ; لأن مثل هذه الحقنة لا يصل منها شيء إلى الجوف من المنافذ المعتادة أصلاً وعلى فرض الوصول، فإنما تصل من المسام فقط وما تصل إليه ليس جوفاً ولا في حكم الجوف. والله أعلم . ينظر : (الفتاوى الإسلامية»(۱ : ۹۰). منحة السلوك (٢ : ١٧٥).
It does not break the fast. He said: 'It does not break the fast' i.e., his fast is not invalidated in this case, such as eating or drinking forgetfully. Analogical reasoning would require it, and the fast would be like in the case of error, but it was abandoned due to what was narrated that a man ate and drank forgetfully during fasting, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to him: 'Complete your fast, for Allah fed you and gave you drink.' This was narrated by the six Imams, al-Daraqutni, Ibn Hibban, and others with similar wordings. If this is established for eating and drinking, it is established for intercourse forgetfully, because it is like them. And the rule for the forgetful person is not like that of the mistaken or coerced person, so that it would be attached to them in ruling and break the fast. As for the case of a wet dream, due to the hadith: 'Three things do not break the fast of the fasting person: cupping, vomiting, and a wet dream.' This was narrated by al-Tirmidhi with a weak chain, and it is supported by the consensus of most imams. (1) As for the ruling of injection in the upper arms or elsewhere, the eminent scholar Muhammad Bakheet issued a fatwa: The condition for something to break the fast is that it reaches the stomach and settles there. What is meant by that is that it enters the stomach, its end is not outside the stomach, and it is not connected to anything outside the stomach, and the reaching to the stomach must be through the usual openings. Because pores and similar openings are not customarily used for something to reach the stomach. From this, it is known that injections under the skin, whether in the upper arms, thighs, buttocks, or any part of the outer body, do not invalidate the fast. Because such an injection does not reach the stomach through the usual openings at all. And even if it did reach, it would only reach through pores, and what it reaches is not the stomach nor is it considered like the stomach. And Allah knows best. See: al-Fatawa al-Islamiyyah (1:90); Minhat al-Suluk (2:175).
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is a sharh explaining the ruling 'lam yuf'tir' (it does not break the fast). The matn states that forgetful eating and drinking do not invalidate the fast. The sharh provides the proof: the famous hadith where the Prophet told a forgetful person to complete his fast because 'Allah fed him and gave him drink.' This hadith is narrated by the six major hadith collectors (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah), al-Daraqutni, Ibn Hibban, and others. The sharh then extends this ruling to intercourse forgetfully by analogy (qiyas). It distinguishes the forgetful person from the mistaken or coerced person, whose fast would be broken. For the case of a wet dream (ihtilam), the proof is the hadith 'Three things do not break the fast: cupping, vomiting, and a wet dream,' though the chain is weak, it is supported by the consensus of most imams. The passage then includes a later fatwa by Muhammad Bakheet on injections: an injection under the skin does not break the fast because it does not reach the stomach through the usual openings; it only goes through pores, which are not considered normal pathways.

Key Terms
ناسياً (naasiyan): Forgetfully, i.e., doing an action without awareness of one's fasting state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for something to break the fast regarding injections?
A) It must reach the stomach through usual openings
B) It must be in the upper arm
C) It must be absorbed into the blood
D) It must be intentional

Key Takeaway
Forgetful eating, wet dreams, and subcutaneous injections do not invalidate the fast in the Hanafi school, based on specific hadith and the condition of reaching the stomach through usual openings.
